LINE 149 | STEP 150 | TYPE PLANNER_RESPONSE | TIME 2026-05-31T05:06:06Z
================================================================================
CONTENT:
I investigated the `500 Internal Server Error` traceback you encountered.

### The Cause
The error was a `KeyError: 'drug_name'` occurring in `fda_service.py`:
```python
local_total = len(self.faers_df[self.faers_df['drug_name'].str.contains(drug_name, case=False, na=False)])
```
When checking the column headers of your local dataset file `faers_master.csv`, the column for the drug name is actually labeled **`drugname`** (all lowercase, no underscore):
`primaryid,caseid,fda_dt,auth_num,age,sex,reporter_country,occr_country,drug_seq,drugname,route,...`

Because of this, trying to reference `'drug_name'` on the pandas DataFrame raised the `KeyError`.

### The Fix
I have updated [fda_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py) (on lines **69** and **151**) to reference `'drugname'` rather than `'drug_name'`:

```diff
-local_total = len(self.faers_df[self.faers_df['drug_name'].str.contains(drug_name, case=False, na=False)])
+local_total = len(self.faers_df[self.faers_df['drugname'].str.contains(drug_name, case=False, na=False)])
```

The Uvicorn dev server has automatically hot-reloaded with this fix. You should now be able to run your `POST /fda/drug-search` and `POST /fda/signal-summary` requests successfully without any internal server errors!

# Refactor Project from Local ChromaDB to ChromaDB Cloud

We are now upgrading the RAG architecture from:

* Local Persistent ChromaDB

TO:

* ChromaDB Cloud

IMPORTANT:
Completely replace the old local ChromaDB logic.

The project must now use:

* ChromaDB Cloud
* Cloud collections
* Cloud vector retrieval
* Multi-collection architecture

========================================================
NEW CHROMADB CLOUD CONFIGURATION
================================

Use the following cloud credentials:

```python
import chromadb

client = chromadb.CloudClient(
    api_key='YOUR_API_KEY',
    tenant='YOUR_TENANT_ID',
    database='PV_AI_Copilot'
)
```

IMPORTANT:
Move these credentials into:
.env

DO NOT hardcode credentials in production code.

========================================================
UPDATE .ENV
===========

Add:

CHROMA_API_KEY=
CHROMA_TENANT=
CHROMA_DATABASE=PV_AI_Copilot

========================================================
REMOVE OLD LOCAL CHROMADB LOGIC
===============================

Remove:

* PersistentClient(path="./chroma_db")
* local chroma_db folder dependency
* local embedded storage logic

The project should now work completely with:

* ChromaDB Cloud

========================================================
NEW CHROMADB ARCHITECTURE
=========================

Create TWO collections:

1. knowledge_base
2. input_documents

========================================================
COLLECTION 1 — knowledge_base
=============================

Purpose:
Persistent pharmacovigilance intelligence knowledge base.

This collection stores:

* CDSCO banned drug PDFs
* UN restricted drug PDFs
* FDA safety documents
* ADR references
* pharmacology references
* drug safety literature
* medical safety intelligence

Workflow:
PDF
↓
Extract Text
↓
Chunk Text
↓
Generate Embeddings
↓
Store in knowledge_base

========================================================
COLLECTION 2 — input_documents
==============================

<USER_REQUEST>
check if we done this,apart from frotned
End-to-End Flow
Step 1 — User Input
User enters adverse event text or uploads a safety document in the Streamlit UI.

Step 2 — Data Extraction
The system extracts important pharmacovigilance entities such as:
Drug name
Adverse event
Indication
Patient age/gender
Dosage
Outcome
Seriousness
Example:
Drug: Amoxicillin
Event: Skin rash
Outcome: Hospitalization

Step 3 — Text Chunking
Large narratives or documents are split into smaller chunks for efficient processing.

Step 4 — Embedding + Vector Database
The extracted chunks are converted into embeddings and stored in a vector database for semantic retrieval.

Step 5 — RAG Retrieval
Relevant chunks related to the adverse event are retrieved using Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG).

Step 6 — AI Analysis
The LLM analyzes the case and generates:
Case summary
Seriousness assessment
Suspected drug-event relationship
Medical insights
Safety observations
Example Output: > “The case indicates a possible serious adverse drug reaction associated with Amoxicillin resulting in severe skin rash and fever.”

Step 7 — Report Generation
The system generates a structured Pharmacovigilance report containing:
Patient details
Drug information
Adverse events
AI-generated narrative summary
Seriousness classification
Reports can be downloaded as:
PDF
Excel
JSON

Step 8 — Final Output in Streamlit UI
The application displays:
Extracted entities
AI-generated summary
Seriousness classification
Structured safety report
Download options

CONTENT:
I have successfully refactored the FDA adverse event query and signal retrieval pipeline to perform strict drug validation and clean up the results as requested.

### Summary of Changes:

1. **New Drug Validator Service**: 
   Created [drug_validator_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/drug_validator_service.py) which takes raw medical entities and isolates verified drug names. It screens out symptoms, diseases, procedures (like *"Abdominal Palpation"*), body parts, and generic hospital nouns by cross-checking against known drug list caches, regulatory datasets (CDSCO/UN), and the local FAERS database.
   
2. **Refactored FDA Intelligence Service**:
   Updated [fda_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py) with:
   * **Validation Guard**: Forces all queries (adverse events, signal summaries, recent/serious records) to go through the drug validator first. Non-drug inputs (like *"Abdominal Palpation"*) are rejected immediately.
   * **MedDRA Term Blacklist**: Filters out administrative, product-use, and device terms (e.g. *Product quality issue, Drug dependence, Product label issue*) from the results.
   * **Reaction Ranking & Deduplication**: Standardizes reaction terms to Title Case, groups by case-insensitive name, and ranks them by count.
   * **Rule-Based Signal Scoring**: Implements thresholds on serious cases and hospitalizations, and automatically boosts the score to `"High"` if severe clinical ADR reactions (like *hepatotoxicity, anaphylaxis, rhabdomyolysis*) are present.

3. **Ingestion & Report Routes Integration**:
   * Updated [analyze.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/routes/analyze.py) to validate candidate drug entities during case ingestion, ensuring only validated drugs are stored in Supabase and indexed in Milvus.
   * Updated [report.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/routes/report.py) to validate drug names when generating the report, passing only clean drug names to the FDA query, RAG context retrieval, and LLM payloads.

---

### E2E Pipeline Verification
I ran the test script [test_fda_pipeline.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/scripts/test_fda_pipeline.py) and **all checks passed successfully**:
* **Input list**: `["Abdominal Palpation", "Methotrexate", "Fatigue", "Rheumatoid Arthritis"]`
* **Isolated Drug list**: `["Methotrexate"]` (successfully filtered out all other items)
* **FDA queries for `Methotrexate`**: Correctly returned clinical reaction lists (excluding blacklisted items) and computed a `"High"` signal score.
* **Invalid Drug inputs**: Correctly returned 0 cases and empty structures.

The FDA signal retrieval pipeline is still selecting incorrect drugs for FDA querying.

"drug_name": "Methotrexate"
}

ROOT CAUSE
==========

The FDA pipeline is currently selecting drugs from:

* raw entities
* cleaned entities
* generic medical terms
* noun phrase extraction

This architecture is incorrect.

========================================================
IMPORTANT ARCHITECTURAL CHANGE
==============================

The FDA query system MUST NEVER use:

* raw SciSpacy entities
* first extracted entities
* noun phrase rankings

for FDA querying.

CORRECT FDA QUERY SOURCE
========================

The FDA service must ONLY use:

structured_output["suspected_drug_information"]["drug_name"]

This becomes the:
SINGLE SOURCE OF TRUTH

========================================================
NEW CORRECT FLOW
================

Raw Extraction
↓
Structured PV Object
↓
Suspected Drug Identification
↓
FDA Search
↓
FDA Signal Retrieval

drug_name = structured_output["suspected_drug_information"]["drug_name"]

* normalize the drug name
* remove dosage text
* trim whitespace

=======

Input:
"Methotrexate 20 mg/week"

"Methotrexate"

STRICT RULE

DO NOT use:

* entities[0]

* first medical noun
* random entity ranking

for FDA querying.

Correct output example:

* FDA querying
* signal analysis
* regulatory validation

Proceed with refactoring the FDA pipeline around this architecture immediately.

### Summary of Enhancements:

1. **Contextual openFDA Queries with Resilient Fallback**:

   * The list is standardized to Title Case, deduplicated, and ranked by the total relevance score.

3. **Report Route Orchestration**:

LINE 1546 | STEP 1522 | TYPE PLANNER_RESPONSE | TIME 2026-06-08T10:06:22Z
================================================================================
CONTENT:
The `api_records_retrieved` count of **100** is due to the API payload limits configured in the backend's query client. 

Here is how the cases count is generated and why you see 100:

### 1. The Retrieval Capping (`api_records_retrieved = 100`)
In [fda_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py), when querying the openFDA endpoint, the backend requests a maximum batch size of 100 individual case report records to keep network payloads fast and lightweight:
```python
api_data = self._query_openfda(api_query, limit=100)
```
The field `"api_records_retrieved"` shows how many full, detailed case objects were actually downloaded and returned in the `raw_api_results` payload (which is capped at `100`).

---

### 2. The Global Total Case Count (`total_cases`)
To show the actual volume of Metformin reports in the FDA database without downloading millions of records, the backend extracts the global total count from the openFDA metadata:
```python
total_api_cases = api_data.get("meta", {}).get("results", {}).get("total", len(api_results))
```
This metadata count (representing the true number of matching cases in FAERS, which can be hundreds of thousands) is added to the local FAERS CSV counts to generate the `"total_cases"` value in the **FDA Signal Summary**.

---

### 3. Local Dataset Count (`local_records_found`)
The `"local_records_found"` count (e.g. `4572` in your Metformin search) is queried directly from your local `faers_master.csv` file using pandas. It scans the entire 558MB dataset on disk to find the exact number of matching drug records:
```python
local_total = len(self.faers_df[self.faers_df['drugname'].str.contains(validated_drug, case=False, na=False)])
```

LINE 1555 | STEP 1532 | TYPE PLANNER_RESPONSE | TIME 2026-06-08T10:18:58Z
================================================================================
CONTENT:
Yes, **it is working completely correctly**. Here is a detailed breakdown of how the counts are generated and why you see those specific numbers.

---

### 1. Why `api_records_retrieved` is exactly `100` in search
In the search route implementation ([fda_service.py:L117](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py#L117)), openFDA API queries are capped with a limit of `100` to prevent excessive bandwidth usage and guarantee fast response times:
```python
api_data = self._query_openfda(api_query, limit=100)
```
Consequently, the API payload contains exactly 100 raw case records. The `api_records_retrieved` field is computed as:
```python
"api_records_retrieved": len(api_results), # Capped at 100
```

---

### 2. How the PV Report Counts are Generated
In the structured adverse event case report (e.g. `768639a5-adf0-4fcc-8222-9fe984d32dba.json`), the fields inside the `fda_signal` block are generated as follows in [fda_service.py:L285-L390](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py#L285-L390):

* **`api_total_cases` (`8511`)**: 
  This is the **true global count** of matching Metformin cases in the entire openFDA database. Instead of counting the 100 fetched records, the backend extracts the total count from the metadata returned by openFDA (`meta.results.total`):
  ```python
  total_api_cases = api_data.get("meta", {}).get("results", {}).get("total", len(api_results))
  ```

* **`local_total_cases` (`4572`)**: 
  This is the total number of records matching Metformin in the local `faers_master.csv` dataset.

* **`total_cases` (`13083`)**: 
  This is the sum of the global API cases and the local database records:
  $$\text{total\_cases} = \text{api\_total\_cases (8511)} + \text{local\_total\_cases (4572)} = 13083$$

* **`serious_cases` (`80`) & `hospitalizations` (`48`)**: 
  These are computed by analyzing the 100 detailed case records retrieved from the API query. Out of the 100 retrieved records, 80 were classified as **Serious** and 48 involved **Hospitalization**. 

---

### Summary
The system is working as designed. The 100 limit is a search payload limit for raw document retrieval, while the metadata fields like `api_total_cases` accurately capture the global size of the FAERS database matching your query.

7: ## Technical Implementations
8: 
9: ### 1. Context-Aware FDA Querying & Fallback
10: * **[fda_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py)**:
11:   * Implemented organ-system classification map (`ORGAN_SYSTEMS`) covering hepatic, renal, dermatological, gastrointestinal, cardiac, neurological, and hematological keywords and MedDRA terms.
12:   * Dynamically scans the case context (text narrative, symptoms, and conditions) to identify target organ systems.
13:   * Automatically builds a boolean AND query for openFDA combining the normalized drug name and target system ADR terms (e.g. `(patient.drug.medicinalproduct:"Methotrexate") AND (patient.reaction.reactionmeddrapt:"hepatotoxicity" OR ...)`).
14:   * Automatically falls back to the drug-only query if the context-specific search yields no results, guaranteeing resilience.
15: 
16: ### 2. Semantic Reaction Relevance Scoring & Ranking
17: * **[fda_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py)**:
18:   * Replaced the generic frequency-only ranking with a clinical **Relevance Score**:
19:     * **Base Score**: Raw FAERS occurrence count.
20:     * **Organ System Match Boost**: Applies a `15.0x` multiplie
<truncated 41 bytes>
the target organ system.
21:     * **Keyword Match Boost**: Applies a `5.0x` multiplier boost for every exact word match from the case symptoms/reactions.
22:   * Standardizes reactions to Title Case and deduplicates them before taking the top 10 ranked by relevance.
23:   * **Context-Aware Signal Score**: Computes the final signal score by checking serious ratios, hospitalizations, severe ADR patterns, and the matching strength of target-system reactions.
24: 
25: ### 3. Route Integrations
26: * **[report.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/routes/report.py)**:
27:   * Extracts the case text narrative, symptoms list, and conditions list from Supabase and passes them to `fda_service_instance.get_fda_signal_summary` as `case_context` to drive context-aware ranking.

I have successfully implemented and verified the FDA/FAERS Visualization Analytics system.

### Key Deliverables Completed:
1. **Visualization Analytics Service ([chart_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/chart_service.py))**:
   * A standalone service that dynamically processes openFDA query records and global statistics to compile five React-ready JSON datasets.
   * Leverages global scaling to adjust cohort proportions (e.g. serious outcomes, reporting trends) to match global totals perfectly.
   * Includes a complete fallback payload generator to handle network/API failures gracefully.
2. **FDA Service Update ([fda_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py))**:
   * Calls `chart_service_instance.generate_charts` right after signal metrics compilation, adding the `"visualizations"` block to the returned dictionary.
3. **Route Integration ([report.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/routes/report.py))**:
   * Pops the `"visualizations"` block out from the FDA payload and embeds it at the root of `report_data` so that it is returned at the root level of the API output and correctly cached in Supabase.

7: ## Technical Implementations
8: 
9: ### 1. Context-Aware FDA Querying & Fallback

11:   * Implemented organ-system classification map (`ORGAN_SYSTEMS`) covering hepatic, renal, dermatological, gastrointestinal, cardiac, neurological, and hematological keywords and MedDRA terms.
12:   * Dynamically scans the case context (text narrative, symptoms, and conditions) to identify target organ systems.
13:   * Automatically builds a boolean AND query for openFDA combining the normalized drug name and target system ADR terms (e.g. `(patient.drug.medicinalproduct:"Methotrexate") AND (patient.reaction.reactionmeddrapt:"hepatotoxicity" OR ...)`).
14:   * Automatically falls back to the drug-only query if the context-specific search yields no results, guaranteeing resilience.

5: ---
6: 
7: ## Technical Implementations
8: 
9: ### 1. Context-Aware FDA Querying & Fallback
10: * **[fda_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py)**:
11:   * Implemented organ-system classification map (`ORGAN_SYSTEMS`) covering hepatic, renal, dermatological, gastrointestinal, cardiac, neurological, and hematological keywords and MedDRA terms.
12:   * Dynamically scans the case context (text narrative, symptoms, and conditions) to identify target organ systems.
13:   * Automatically builds a boolean AND query for openFDA combining the normalized drug name and target system ADR terms (e.g. `(patient.drug.medicinalproduct:"Methotrexate") AND (patient.reaction.reactionmeddrapt:"hepatotoxicity" OR ...)`).
14:   * Automatically falls back to the drug-only query if the context-specific search yields no results, guaranteeing resilience.
15: 
16: ### 2. Semantic Reaction Relevance Scoring & Ranking
17: * **[fda_service.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/services/fda_service.py)**:
18:   * Replaced the generic frequency-only ranking with a clinical **Relevance Score**:
19:     * **Base Score**: Raw FAERS occurrence count.
20:     * **Organ System Match Boost**: Applies a `15.0x` multiplier boost to reaction terms that belong to the target organ system.
21:     * **Keyword Match Boost**: Applies a `5.0x` multiplier boost for every exact word match from the case symptoms/reactions.
22:   * Standardizes reactions to Title Case and deduplicates them before taking the top 10 ranked by relevance.
23:   * **Context-Aware Signal Score**: Computes the final signal score by checking serious ratios, hospitalizations, severe ADR patterns, and the matching strength of target-system reactions.
24: 
25: ### 3. Route Integrations
26: * **[report.py](file:///Users/affu01/GRAD_PROJ_NEW/backend/app/routes/report.py)**:
27:   * Extracts the case text narrative, symptoms list, and conditions list from Supabase and passes them to `fda_service_instance.get_fda_signal_summary` as `case_context` to drive context-aware ranking.
28: 
29: ---
30:

32:

35: ```bash
